RATING: 8
Smash up is the best of both worlds. It's a deckbuilder that doesn't require any thought in how to build your deck. It's a "take that" game that stays well balanced throughout many expansions. The only thing that this game needs is a randomizer for picking factions. Other than that, and the fiddly power modifier tokens, it's damn near perfect. It teaches fast, and can play 2 or 4 easily. I've even played 6 player battles (although, they stretched everyone's patience by the end). I will say, some cards and timing are poorly worded and/or fiddly, leading to the loudest player getting their wish. I rarely can play this game without looking up a rule/combo issue on BGG. Other than that, I really enjoy this game - and have yet to meet an expansion faction I didn't come to love.

Also owned: Awesome Level 9000, [-]Science Fiction Double Feature[/-], Pretty Pretty, Monster Smash, & It's Your Fault.

=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 9
[COLOR=#FFFFFF][BGCOLOR=#FF9933][b]aaj's FAVORITE SHUFFLEBUILDER[/b][/BGCOLOR][/COLOR]
[I]tl;dr When Smash Up is firing on all cylinders, it's a quick-playing competition/cooperation game that revolves around the special abilities that all these wacky card combos can create. When you really do know what you're doing, this produces a very enjoyable experience that plays in just under an hour and produces a lot of laughs all around.[/I]
[COLOR=#CCCCFF]____________________________[/COLOR]

[b]Read the full review [url=https://boardgamegeek.com/article/24594456]here[/url].[/b]

What can I say? SmashUp is one of my top games. I've found SmashUp to be a great "gateway" game that really stretches people and gets them interested in board games. The fact that there's a million factions to choose from means that people generally can end up with something that looks interesting to them. 

The game holds up well, with good replayability and variety, especially as you add on further expansions and factions. Most factions don't change the rules at all, but offer you more choices of special abilities and card powers that will give you an edge against other players. 

In SmashUp, the basic concept is that you pick two factions: say, Alien-Horses or Super Spy-Dinosaurs, and mash them together to create a 40-card deck of unique ability. This is a shuffle-building game, not a collectible card game, so no player is disadvantaged by not having rare, powerful cards. Instead, everyone gets a level playing field as they draft two factions from the same pool. 

Once chosen, players compete to score points on bases by playing both minions and actions. Minions give you power at a certain base, and actions manipulate bases, minions, and other players. The first player to 15 victory points wins the game! 

Generally, folks who like serious, engine-building games won't be a fan of this sort of game (although personally, I appreciate both types). SmashUp is silly, madcap, and crazy, and the cards are often cartoony or filled with jokes. But as a mid-casual gamer, I really enjoy the mechanic of choosing a good combination and crushing the competition. 

SmashUp is always a favorite at our game nights and we haven't come close to using up all the possible combinations (though one poor guy has a knack for the worst combos: hello Cyborg Ape-Time Travellers!)

I recommend SmashUp simply because it's rollicking good fun with a lot of variety. Originally, I wanted to add every expansion all at once, but have realized that a huge part of the metagame of Smash Up comes with knowledge -- knowing what your opponents pick, how those decks work, and how to counter them. As such, we've slowly added back expansions, after selling off a ton about a year ago.

RATING: 5
A well thought idea with a bit awkward execution. I really enjoyed choosing factions to create my own unique draw deck. The asymmetrical setup makes the game much more interesting and adds longevity, I reckon. The art is a bit childish but works. Figuring out the best way to play your hand and creating combos is fun, BUT the very same part is the downfall of Smash Up as well. You simply have too many cards in your hand and there are too many things going on the table in parallel which forms a too vast of an option space for a game that should be played at a very fast pace. Sure you can throw cards casually without giving your moves much of a thought but you would miss the point of the game entirely. There is an easy fix to the problem, i.e., reduce the hand limit by half and remove some of the point cards fought over from the table, but I must admit that this might cause some balance issues if you just keep drawing wrong types of cards.
 
But anyways, Smash Up offers enough fun to justify its existence despite the rough edges.

RATING: 5
I have it a 5 for a few reasons. Some of which is a shortcoming in which I have not play this game more times.

It's very light for most gamers and is One of those simple math game where bigger is better. Interactions comes with various card effects and special action cards that does things to the game but essentially changes the values on cards that eventually assist in scoring.

There are other light cards games that plays similarly, this just provides multiple 'base' options instead of just fighting for 1.

Theme wise was really low as I did not really bother what faction I was playing, just trying to get cards to interact was more important.

Overall, a good gateway game, but not the kind of math game I was looking for.

RATING: 4
I do not like this game. Its theme is attractive and the game-play is simple, but so dull it makes me physically ill. Every turn you play two cards, sometimes they help you but most of the time its because you've got nothing better. Then at the end of your turn you draw two cards. Super simple, incredibly boring. The downtime between player turns is way too long for a game that should take 40 minutes. I've played 6 or 7 games of this and 1.5 hour games are apparently pretty common, not just in my group but in others I have seen play. In that time I could play Core Worlds or 3 games of Dominion. I do not enjoy this game, some people will and that is fine, but personally I can't stand it.

RATING: 7
I was very surprised by how much fun this game is for two players.  Even though I typically enjoy playing with larger groups, I think this is best 1v1.  We use a spinner to keep track of how close we are to breaking each base, which cuts down on the constant addition that can slow things down a bit.  The base set is a ton of fun and you absolutely don't need any expansions (although you will probably buy some anyway).  There's certainly power creep going on, as the pirates in the base set are by far the weakest group, but many of my favorite factions are in here.

The "shufflebuilding" game Smash Up starts with a simple premise: Take the twenty-card decks of two factions, shuffle them into a forty-card deck, then compete to smash more Bases than your opponents! Each faction brings a different game mechanism into play â pirates move cards, zombies bring cards back from the discard pile, dinosaurs have huge power â and every combination of factions brings a different play experience.

Its decisions can range from being somewhat shallow to a just a bit of depth. Everyone is flinging around silly and possibly broken powers every turn to completely change the state of the game. Worth a laugh and bit of thought, but not a ton more.

RATING: 6.5
I've only played once. I'd seen it being played on TableTop and seen some reviews of the cards, and it seemed like a fairly light, silly game.

But it wasn't. It plays like Magic or something of that ilk. It's not a light game. You have to sit there and think and strategize based on your hand and the condition of the board. Not at all what I was expecting, but that's actually more to my taste than it would have been if it had been a light, silly game.

But I sense that there's a problem with that.

We were playing at 3 players, and it felt like with more players than that, the game would be a bit too long between turns. So I wouldn't want to play it 4 players. At 2 players, I'd rather play Magic since that has more interesting decks and mechanisms. So this is really limited to a 3 player game. I don't think I'd want to own a 3 player only game.

And, a thing with Magic is that deck "strength" is a pretty loose term. There are certainly decks that are clearly more powerful than your average pre-constructed pack, or what-have-you. But that doesn't mean that they will win against every other deck (being played by a competent player) of a weaker strength. Some decks are just inherently weak against certain things.

With Mashup, assuming that they have done a good job of balancing everything, it seems likely that all of the decks are on average of equal "strength". But I think that for any particular matchup, they're not going to be equal, because one will be weak to that particular style of play.

With Magic, you can buy duelling decks or construct decks that balance well against each other. With Mashup, unless you hunt up historical data, you're not going to know whether the decks you have in play are going to be competitive against each other. And since there's 3 of them in play, having them be competitive against both of the other 2 is going to be a pretty tall order.

Personally, I don't care about winning too much. I think I won the one game that I played, and I'd happily play it again. But I would probably have to recommend against buying this if you do care about winning as there might be some balance issues, unless you play lots of games across many pairings. And I would recommend against buying it unless you expect to be in a lot of 3-player situations.
=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-

RATING: 8
Simple and fun. Is a great game for people who like card games for the combos they can pull off from them (i.e. people who have played CCGs like magic and are looking to pull off cool moves with cards). The game is really easy to teach (1 minion, 1 action unless you do something special) and has a lot of really fun artwork that help to get people in the game. Can be a bit fiddly as there will be a lot of cards spread out on the board, so be sure to check out the really cool base mats in the files section. Overall, a very fun filler for people who aren't looking for something too heavy.

RATING: 8
Initial Impression: I love the simplicity of this game. Each faction plays differently and modifies the game mechanisms in thematic ways. Mixing 2 different factions into one deck makes for alot of variability in the play. Add to that the variable battlegrounds and you're in for tons of replay ability. The mechanisms of the game are similar to Bloodbowl Team Manager, Battleline, or Omen: Reign of War in the sense that you will deploy your units to various battlefields in the hopes of gaining a majority. Deploying the units will trigger various effects, which is where much of the fun occurs. Games don't last too long and it seems that its a close race in the end.

=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 3
Zombie-Ninjas sound like fun, right? How about Robot-Dinosaurs, or Pirate-Wizards? The concept is interesting as you try to blend the talents of 2 different geeky factions in order to conquer different geeky locations. When I read the rules I was psyched because it sounded light, fast and fun too. Unfortunately, when we played it didn't meet those expectations. While the rules are simple, the card effects and base effects just make things confusing. With a group of gamers this would probably all be second nature, but with non-gamers it quickly gets overwhelming (particularly because of the fact that different cards can be played at different moments in the game.) Then there's the constant adding up of cards and modifiers to check if locations are complete each turn. Finally, my OCD goes into overdrive with these games where there is no logical place to play all the cards. Ideally you want to read all the abilities/values of all the cards splayed off all 4 sides of all 4 bases, but this causes one row to run into another, and it just drives me batty. With all these little issues it just ends up being tedious rather than fun. If all the players had a level of familiarity with the cards it would flow, and be fast. I can see that potential in the system, but I'm not sure I have the right group to get there.

=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 7.5
Smash Up, as the name implies, sees players taking two unique factions, represented by small decks of minions and spells, and shuffling them together to make their own personal deck. With a witty and goofy theme to it, this can range from awesome (robot dinosaurs) to ridiculous (shark princesses). The base game is decent but the fun really comes out from getting the expansions that tickle your fancy. 

The gameplay is fairly simple, try to have area majority on locations, using minions, once their point limit is reached to score the most, and use the spells to further your cause in other ways. Perhaps some faction combinations are really too powerful to be countered, but for the most part the game is incredibly well balanced.

My only 2 complaints with the game are really one connected one. Keeping track of everything on each location, with special powers taken into consideration can be very hard to manage, and min-max types of players should be avoided because of this. With that being said, the game works best at 3 players, 2 can often become, who's deck combo is a bit better, and with 4 it's just too much to keep track of and too much downtime.

RATING: 9
Before reading further on, I'd like to emphasize on the fact that I completely adore this game.
At the same time, I know that people read reviews to get a good impression of what is good/bad about the particular game. Thus, both the comment and the review will be critical ones. 

The good:
   The mechanism. I understand that the idea of a simple mechanism with complexity coming from the components is somewhat frustrating to a handful of players, however, I have never had a problem with that. 
   The artwork. 
   The references. 

The bad:
   No components are provided for keeping track of the scoring. Of course, no one banned the old pen/paper duo and the problem was resolved with the first expansion. At the same time, when you buy a game, you expect to get everything one needs in order to start playing. The little 

The ugly:
   The chemistry between factions. A major flaw of the game is the fact that not all faction work great together. This might harm the first impression for new players, specially if there is no one experienced to help them pick out the factions. I am calling major flaw on this one because I do not see how it could be prevented with any kind of modifications.

In conclusion, while Smash Up is not the next Carcassonne of the board gaming community, it is capable of forming its own dedicated fanbase thanks to its outstanding pros.

=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 7
Smash Up plays a lot like a chaotic version of Battle Line/Schotten Totten, if you know either of those games.

If you don't know either of those games, in Smash Up, you're playing cards to bases.  When the number of cards at a base reaches a certain level, the base scores, giving players points for having cards there.  You ideally want more points at a base than the other players.  Once you score a certain number of points, you win.

The fun is in all of the special abilities of the cards, and how those special abilities can interact.  The base game comes with 8 races of cards, like robots, dinosaurs, pirates, ninjas, zombies, etc.  Each of these races has a different deck of cards with different special abilities.  At the beginning of the game, you take two races and shuffle them together to create your deck.  So, one game you might be playing with an army of pirates and zombies, and the next game you might get dinosaurs and aliens.  So, each game will play differently for you depending on the race combination you get.

The bases are also all different, and each have their own special ability either when you add a card to a base, or when the base scores, etc.  The different base abilities can also interact with the deck abilities in different (and sometimes wacky) ways!

Overall, a neat little game.  Pretty beer & pretzel weight.  My only caution is that I'll probably exclusively play it as a three player game.  It gets really chaotic with four, and the downtime can get to be a bit much if the card combos start getting really wacky.  Other than that, good stuff! 
=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-

RATING: 6.5
I played in a four-player game of Smash Up at TactiCon 2012 in Denver. Having heard about the buzz from GenCon, I was eager to give it a go.

My deck was the Alien Dinosaurs, and I saw more of the alien cards in my play-through. The game took a while because it was new to three out of the four of us.

I love the theme - how can you not? The mechanics, though, didn't really do it for me. It was a little boring when the Robot Wizard player had these complex, drawn-out turns, drawing and playing tons of cards, while my turns were very quick - drop a creature, play an action, done. 

The game didn't feel unbalanced; the final score was 15-11-11-8, so it wasn't a blowout (and the long-turn player actually finished in last place). The problem was that it just wasn't much fun. I was looking for a way to just make it end rather than to win. That's not a good sign!

Awesome theme, great art, so-so game play.

=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 5
Based on 1 play with 4 players:

There's so much in this game that I hate in principle, but taken as a whole it's more enjoyable than the sum of its parts.

I think that all speaks to how well the decks are designed. There's lots of fun little synergies that just feel good to pull off. 

That said, since you start with complete decks it is nowhere near as satisfying as any game where you build your combinations as you play (deckbuilding games, or something like San Juan or hell, getting into board games, even stuff like Last Will). There's no greater strategy other than hoping you draw the right cards. 

For that reason, Smash Up strikes me as something that might make a good intro to the whole combo-building mechanic. For seasoned players, though, Smash Up doesn't have much to offer.

Fair warning also: I can see a real potential for this game to drag. Like many content-driven games you wind up drawing a bunch of cards (inevitably, sometimes, during your turn) and have to spend awhile reading through all of them and figuring out what to do with 'em. Nearly every turn for us started with "uhh wait hang on I'm still figuring this out". If you're going to play a lot with the same decks the problem will eventually sort itself out, but in the interim be prepared for some waiting.

=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 8
[b]Includes the Awesome Level 9000 and Pretty Pretty Smash Up expansions.[/b]

I traded for Smash Up looking for a great lunchtime filler game. And, after one play, I'd say it delivers exactly as I hoped. Easily playable within an hour, with a theme that is lighthearted and absurd, and tons of replayability based on all the potential pairings.

It's one of those games where the core rules are simple but the complexity and tension stems from all the different card powers and abilities. It does add some complexity as players try to figure out the options... all varying based on their hand of cards. But I suspect it gets smoother with familiarity.

Probably not for those groups that balk at "take that" card games, but for a quick card game with interesting choices, this looks like a solid bet.

The game mechanics are whacky and chaotic, usually in a positive way, and there is something especially fun about creating a faction combination. It's neither a very strategic game, nor a very casual one, but it is a great choice if you're in the right mood for it. I also have to comment on how impressed I am that there are this many factions and faction or combination seems to be excessively more or less powerful than another. A lot of work was clearly put into balancing this game.
I'd definitely recommend getting at least one expansion for it though, especially if you want to play with the maximum number of players (just a couple more factions will add a lot more variety).

RATING: 8
This game is the whole package: fantastic to teach newbies but fun enough to maintain an expert's interest. The box is filled with small decks themed around different "clans," and you pick any two to shuffle together. Our first battles pitched Zombie Wizards vs Robotic Dinosaurs, along with Ninja Pirates vs Alien Leprechauns. Each side brings something unique to the table (the zombies bring back cards from the discard, the wizards can look at their future draws) and the combinations, while not always the most effective, are always fun. Laughs the first few games, but then the musing on strategies sets in. Expansions offer more clans, and the original box here has the space to accomodate all future purchases.

RATING: 4
I really wanted to like this game, but...

It doesnt do for me what i wanted it to be: A not too complicated "action paced" card game. The name "Smash Up" suggested some action to me, maybe i didnt inform myself well enough beforehand. However, playtime gets too long for me with several players. Game concept is too boring for me for the lenght of play. If you play with 2 players it might be ok, but for me, there are better 2p games...

With several players i found it hard to play to your strategy because it was too hard to time destroying a base with like 3 people having turns after you. Nobody will prepare it for you for an easy catch. Thats the main reason for me it feels boring: you have to play nice combos in order to get a base within the game limitations (one monster, one action).

Cards have alot of text and it is hard to keep track of all the bases HP, players Victory points and with several players in game: all the effects that might trigger on  permanent cards. Which it makes it feel its a game for heavy gamers while i felt it should be a light game cause of the "light" rules.

Overall that makes the game too chewy for me.

Personal Summary:
--------
Pros: Overall Theme and general game idea, Artwork, travel size
Cons: Balance Issues depending on faction combos, too long, too less action, too much to keep track off for this type of game.

RATING: 6.4
The rules are pretty simple here - play an action and play a minion card.  If one of the base cards has enough minion points to hit its target, then it scores, and points go out to the top 3 players at that base.

One of the real problems here is the complete luck of the draw - even the best cards are worthless if you get them at the wrong time.  Or that turn when you have a lot of actions and not a single minion?  Rats.

While I like the art, humor and themes used in this game, the high degree of luck can be a real drag.  I'll play it again, but not a game I need to own.

RATING: 3
We're big fans of Guillotine and Unexploded Cow, but this game by the same designer fell flat. 
The biggest problem is information overload (so many cards each with different abilities); the need to calculate/recalulate all the time is a big pain. Seems like this is the cardboard version of a solid tablet game.

The concept, theme, and prodution are remarkable. The core mechanism is an overly familiar place-the-minions-on-the-bases area influence design. A recent game that did this a lot better is Blood Bowl Team Manager (although Smash Up scales better to a wider range of player numbers). An old game that did this in a more clever way is FFG's Orcz.

RATING: 6
A fun and easy to teach game. The theme draws new players in, and the mechanics are quick to learn and straightforward. As most people will point out, some decks are much better than others, and some combinations will simply never win. This becomes far more prevalent with the expansions, all of which have one deck that's incredibly overpowered, two that are relatively balanced with the base game and one deck that is virtually useless.

For its price, I'd say it is a decent game and worth picking up for a small game group. However, it does have its flaws and can become very repetitive if overplayed.

RATING: 3
Players shuffle two themed decks together (e.g. Aliens and Robots, or Dinosaurs and Pirates), then play cards in an attempt to influence common bases, and score victory points off them.  Silly, simple game where players may play a minion, and an action, to try to place themselves in a scoring position.  Minions and actions have special effect text which ranges from mildly useful to wildly chaotic.  Bases also come with their own special rules, which means there is a lot of reading to be done, especially in early games.  Cute art, and great, cooky theme.  Unfortunately the game plays like a chaotic, multi-player Schotten-Totten.  Hang on for 75 minutes (way too long for this type of game) and hope you get left alone.  Okay, if you're in the mood for silly.

RATING: 10
Smash Up is the game I have picked up and put down more than any other board game. It looks and sounds great, but somehow I always managed to justify not buying this game.

one week I had no other options on the table and my board game allowance wasn't about to go towards paying a bill, so I broke down and purchased this gem.

Then I felt dumb for putting it down all those other times. So much wasted time not playing this game. What a great game. So much diversity to choose from. Pop culture factions that don't feel ham-fisted into the game. Each faction has a play style that works with the theme they represent. 

Strategy, fun, game mechanics, High quality art... I know a score above 6 on this site jeopardizes a gamer's geek-cred but I find it near impossible that anyone would not enjoy this game.

RATING: 9
I love this game.  It feels like a deck builder where your decks have already been built and now you're playing them at the height of their power.  Watching the card abilities mesh with each other is a blast.  Combos that don't seem like much can blossom hands that produce amazing results.  My Alien Pirate combo cleared 3 bases in one turn, and then a fourth the following round to win the game.  

Yes, the game is designed for tearing your opponents down as much as you try to build yourself own minions up. Don't play if you want a pacifist game. 
Yes, there is some down time as others think and strategize. Yes, you need to keep track of all the various abilities on the table to optimize your deck's effectiveness.
But, as an ex-Magic player, I don't mind the mental tracking of the powers and cards on the board.  I prefer a game that has some cerebral taxing to build up your best punch.  I don't want a game that has me look at my cards and immediately know the best play.
The game is best with players (obviously) who know the factions they are playing.  Otherwise there will be time taken as new cards are reviewed.  
This isn't Yahtzee.  
We play a King of the Mountain version.  The winner can use his/her combo deck until defeated, and then they need to create a new one.  The defeated create new Smash Ups to take on the current King of the Hill.  Forces us to continuously explore new combos.

=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 6.75
The "brospeak" wording of the rules at first made me wary.   This one has surprising complexity for what seems like a theme pandering to the lowest common denominator, the kitchen sink of genre games. I consider it a more developed cousin to Munchkin. While both are steeped in the chaos of "take that" abilities and effects, the latter subjects players to far less opportunity to win on individual merit.

What might throw off casual gamers is a fair amount of numbers tracking, essentially which bonuses apply to which cards, in which locations, and to which players. Each turn presents a veritable litany of pluses and minuses through which players must navigate.

FYI - My first four player game might have been quicker if we'd played some rules correctly:

1) There is supposed to be one more base than there are players. This would have meant less squabbling over territory and some cards being slightly more powerful.

2) Once scoring begins on a base, it continues EVEN IF total minion power falls below the Breakpoint, and if minions that get to move to other bases afterward would cause those bases to score, they do before the next turn begins. This would certainly have aided faster scoring and a sooner end.

3) This rule was relevant during one score: Players involved in a tie each score the same Victory Points, but use up as many succeeding places on the base as there are tying players. So, if two players tie for highest minion power on a scoring base, they both receive the 1st place point value. The player with the next highest power in that scenario gets the 3rd place point value, not the 2nd. If four players have minions on a scoring base, and three of them tie for highest power, those three get the 1st place value and the fourth gets no points!

RATING: 6
(Rating includes expansion: [thing=134726]Awesome Level 9000[/thing])

Smash Up is a fun game, but it suffers from a few problems.

1) It can be a bit intimidating to get started despite the easy rules because each player picks two factions at the beginning of the game and knowing which factions work well together is very important. Of course, knowing the factions themselves is also very helpful so you know what the faction does and where it shines.

2) Keeping track of everything can be a nuissance when there are numerous bases, creatures and actions on the table. Using dice or other measures to keep track of the total strength helps, but there are still other effects that might influence the status.

3) Smash Up is best played with 3 and only 3. With 2 players the scoring of the bases doesn't work at all because you get second place very easily by just placing one creature there and you spend way too much to gain first place. With 4 players, it just takes forever as there are even more effects in play and the downtime becomes a real problem.

I once heard someone saying that the idea of Smash Up is better than the game itself and I have to agree. For one, I wish it would play faster. There is a lot of back and forth so it can take a while until you actually score a base.

RATING: 7
A neat alternative to the collectible card/deck-building market.  Mix A + B or B + C or even A + C, there is your deck!  For anyone who retired from MtG because building a deck was such an arduous process, this is an interesting, lighter alternative.

Definitely some combos are better than others and some decks offer better synergy but it's fun to try them and see what happens; if you are worried about certain combinations, do a draft style game.

Don't expect the depth and strategy of MtG, just take Smash-Up for what it is.  A light-hearted area control/pseudo-deck-builder game.

=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 7
A surprisingly fun game.  I thought for sure I wasn't going to like this game based on comments that I had read comparing it to Munchkin. The game is very simple to pickup and yet there is enough complexity to make the game require a great deal of thought to play correctly.  You get more resources in cards than you tend to be able to keep up with using, so the actions that you take each turn matter quite a lot and you are faced with decisions that actually matter on a frequent basis.  A lot of other games I have played make me feel like the games are playing themselves and I am just carrying out the actions for the game.  Smash Up actually gave me the feeling like I was in control of the game instead of the other way around.

Theme: Awesome theme with puns all around
Relevant Choices: How you play the game pretty directly effects your likelihood of winning the game.
Card Art & design: Great artwork
Replay: Tons of replay through the potential deck combinations.
Learning Curve: Low learning curve, easy to pick up and play. 
Promotion of thought: Lots of potential synergies between cards and factions providing for a good deal of planning and strategy
Random Element: Card draw and faction combinations, but the random element of the game is very manageable.
Box: The box comes with a ton of open spaces for adding new factions to the game through expansions.  Does require sleeves to have the factions fit snug though.

=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 6
Its deck building and yet its not deck building.  The core game comes with eight "races", each with their own deck.  Take two decks and shuffle them together and those are your cards.  Other players do the same with other "races".  Then you battle.  Each "race" has its own style.  Zombies help you get cards out of the discard.  Dinosaurs have sheer power.  Bots amplify each other, etc.  Its a nice light-hearted game that no one takes too seriously.  There's 56 different deck combinations in the core game, with tons of expansions to make that even better.  And the basic box has plenty of room for extra expansions in it, too.  So there's good replay-ability.
=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 5

RATING: 7

=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 7
Pros
-Less mathy than I thought (see cons)
-Fun mashing two decks together
-Races feel fairly unique
-Simple to play and teach
-Nice artwork, fun card names occasionally
-Lots of cards, lots of replayability
-Ability to do combos (not too advanced)
-Lots of expansions, lots of recognizable, unique races

Cons
-A little bit mathy, needing to occasionally calculate and compare numbers is annoying, especially numerous modifiers
-Spatially can be a bit messy, have to be organized in how you arrange cards around bases...lots of cards makes play space confusing
-Lots of card text (even though its mostly simple) makes it hard for new players initially, also slows down gameplay as you need to keep checking what other people played, and recheck as you go
-Alliances/king making can be a problem
-Game can go on longer than one may expect
-Easy to get screwed over by another player last minute right before a base is scored with little counter-play (esp in larger group games)
-Deck combinations are not balanced, some will be stronger than others
-Base game doesn't come with VP markers (fixed in expansions)

RATING: 8
Very simple shuffle building game. Take any two factions, shuffle the decks together. You're competing to conquer bases which require a certain amount of power collectively to score. Each turn you can play one creature and one action. All the expansions just add more decks and more variety. Doesn't take long to play, but recommend it with three or four and having one less base in play than recommended forces more interaction and makes things go faster.

RATING: 6
Interesting little card game, which can really be fun when played with the right folks in the right setting. It's clearly meant to be a light, beer and pretzels kind of game but it can often last way longer than I want it to.

The factions are too unbalanced (the zombies are tons of fun to play but pretty annoying to play against) and there's too much randomness and chaos for my tastes. 

If it were possible to move through your deck faster, I probably would've enjoyed it more. It seemed like I would frequently end up with a hand full of either minions OR actions and would get sort of jammed up since there was no way to discard unless your hand went over 10 cards or an action card granted you that ability and usually while that was happening my opponent would be running the table so that became very frustrating.

And the fact that the base game doesn't come with a way to track your victory points or the minions' power on each base is pretty lame, it just needlessly extends the game because you have to stop and count the power up each turn.

The art is really nice. The theme is fun but I get roughly the same experience from King of Tokyo, which is a much more fun game, in my opinion.

Also, this was the first (and, so far, only) game that my wife declared that she hated.

Traded it away.

=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 4
This game is a throwback to my 80's Ameritrash boardgaming youth. If I was still 13-14 then SMASH UP would be one of my favorite games of all time. But now, even as a filler or a quick nostalgic gaming lark, it doesn't work at all.

The game embraces chaos, randomness, luck of the draw, take that. It's a LCG-lite with variable and asymmetrical powered decks that combine to spontaneously generate wacky and usually wildly over- or underpowered combos and lots of imbalance depending on the factions you select. 

There is very little depth and control in the gameplay. You aren't actually constructing, you are combining two preset decks which don't interact with each other at all - another knock on the supposed "theme." If the pirates and ninjas, for example, could interact with each other within your deck in meaningful ways, it would have helped. 

Because it's CCG/LCG the game is text-heavy and has timing/fiddliness issues - so while it looks super-awesome to kids, it's not really a great game for younger, non-Magic savvy players.

It played like the worst bits of Strange Synergy and Fluxx. Overstays its welcome - especially with 3 or 4 players.

Quarriors or Epic Spell Wars of the Battle Wizards scratch this Ameri-itch much better - there's randomness and combos, but there is also strategy, balance and the dice mitigate or at least justify the luck/random element.

The game theme is like a B-movie at a drive-in theater. The presentation and price point insures that this light chaotic romp will be popular - as it already is on BGG. Especially with expected expansions (the box insert already has 8 more deck slots for future factions). 

My game rating reflects the admiration at AEG's marketing, game theme, and presentation.

=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 7
Smash Up's theme is good nonsensical fun. Things are fighting other things. That's all you need to know. The illustrations are really quite lavish and stay away from being overly cartoony, despite the lightness of the game. The box has ample room for the inevitable expansions. From a production standpoint, this one is a winner.

The gameplay consists of fighting over various locations in the center of the board. Each location grants points to the player with the highest total strength of his cards played at said location. Once a total strength threshold is reached, these points are awarded, and the first player to a set number of points is the winner of the game. In practice, this ends up being a lot of addition and calculation, and never really feels like a real battle. The creature cards never really attack each other. 

The hook of the game is that your deck consists of two different factions of creatures shuffled together, from the available 8. So you might have pirates and zombies fighting against your opponents ninjas and dinosaurs. Sometimes these combinations can be very complimentary, and other times not. The deck can be quite literally stacked against you from the start depending on how you draw. Additionally, some of the factions focus on discarding certain types of cards from play. If your opponents deck does not have that type of cards, many of your draws will be dead weight. 

All of this randomness could be forgivable since it is such a quick and light game. Unfortunately, the combat itself offers very little opportunity for combos, clever card play, tough choices, or sacrifice. Hand management is almost irrelevant. For the first few games, you will be caught up laughing at the theme and artwork, but once you have seen it, there is no real fun to fall back on.

RATING: 6.9
Combine two factions to make your own deck; play cards (minions and actions, max of one per turn) to capture points from locations. First to 15 points wins.

Not all factions are equal, but most are interesting. Combining with any expansion increases the possibilities. In the base box, there is room to fit two expansions. Maybe three if you take out the ones no one ever uses (like Trickster).

Whenever we play, we often give each player 3 random factions and they pick which two they want to play with. It pushes us to break out of what we tend to gravitate towards and try the other factions out.

RATING: 5
This was the game that first got me into hobby board gaming, so it holds a special spot in my collection.

Such a fun card game that attempts to mix every geek genre out there! Pirates, Dinosaurs, Zombies, Robots, Aliens...the list goes on. 

This introduces a new mechanic in a world of 'deck-building' games called, 'shuffle-building.' You simply take two faction decks and shuffle them together. So one person could be playing Dinosaur Ninjas (or Ninja Dinosaurs depending on your philosophical bent) vs Zombie Wizards. Play goes back and forth, competing for first place points on Base Cards.

Best played as a 2-player game, though it can go up to 4.

La idea es que cualquier jugador puede asignar unidades en esas bases con el fin de sobrepasar su resistencia. Las cartas son de dos tipos: los esbirros y las acciones. Los esbirros son los que realmente se juegan en las bases y la mayorÃ­a de ellos tienen una habilidad especial que se activa cuando se ponen en la mesa. Las acciones permiten al jugador jugar esbirros extra, devolver cartas al mazo de robo, aumentar la fuerza de los esbirros, evitar acciones especiales de los contrincantes... En definitiva: hacer combos.

Es adictivo, es caÃ³tico: si; pero parece bien equilibrado si juegas cada facciÃ³n a lo que se supone que mejor sabe hacer.

PROS: Curva de aprendizaje asequible para novatos. Mucha diversidad para elegir. Cada facciÃ³n tiene un estilo de juego que casa con su tema (dinosaurios, destruir; ninjas, efectos sorpresa....) RÃ¡pido y fÃ¡cil ademÃ¡s de tener la informalidad necesaria para que nadie se lo tome muy en serio si pierde.

Las primeras veces es demasiado largo al no conocer nadie las cartas, los efectos y sus consecuencias. RATING: 4
I was so excited to play this game. I heard that this game that features a ton of asymmetrical teams that can be mixed together making unique combinations which would make each game feel fresh. Thatâs a fantastic idea to work a game around. 

The problem is that I found the gameplay to be slow paced and boring. When you look at the phenomenal artwork on the box and the cards, it gives you the idea that the game is going to be about these different factions fighting one another. But the gameplay never feels like youâre a part of a battle. Each of the characters that you throw on the table just becomes a part of a math equation, and each action card adds a variable that you have to account for a turn or two. After each player lays down a card, you have to add up all of the numbers again and again. 

I know that a lot of games rely on similar number-dependent mechanics but what makes this game worse than other games is that this one doesnât seem to hide it at all. It just feels like math homework, and itâs not very fun.

RATING: 8
A deceptively deep card game that's easy to learn the basics of.  The 8 difference factions all offer wildly different gameplay mechanics, making for several interesting deck combinations.

Some faction combinations create some glaring imbalances in the game that can easily be exploited by players who are more familiar with the game.

Overall a very fun card game that's more structured and focused than a game like Munchkin, but not nearly as complicated and counter-intuitive as games like Nightfall.

By description, I should not like this game but the silliness in it is pretty attractive. With new players the downtime is excessive so I would suggest a game to fewer points so everyone can familiarize with the cards.

RATING: 5
Smash up is a cool concept and the first and only shuffle building game I've ever played and owned. 

My gripes are more with the concept of shuffle building than they are with smash up itself. 

Overall I love the factions and seeing how the devs brought them all to life. I love the intricacies and the simple and straightforward gameplay and setup that it has and I love the art to death!!!!!

What I don't like: 
New players get hosed and pick factions that may not work well together. Which leads to the next gripe of players are able to pick factions that just don't do much comparatively.
You have to play a lot to see how the factions work together, but there's really not a high degree of replayability. I mean the factions all do what you'd expect but there's only so many times that robots upon robots upon robots is fun to lose to/win with. Because the driving faction typically is what will determine how the deck plays.
Gameplay can be slow and you wait long periods of time to get to you... Plus due to the deck size... There are turns sometimes where you don't do much... Action packed would not describe this game.
Overall you need a sharp group that plays quickly and precisely to play this well.

RATING: 2.5
Disappointing game, expected a better experience.

The problem is that the game is full of cards that need to be read. At the same time, this is a light card game with a lot of chaos. Both ends simply do not combine, since you must read through all the cards in play and in your hand while keeping it light-hearted.

Furthermore, it's a pain in the ass to keep track whether or not the break point of each base has been reached. Too much repetitive math involved for a light game. I use tokens to keep track but that's still not good enough.

All this math and card reading drag the game down and detract from its fun chaotic purpose.

Finally, the game doesn't even come with tokens for VP. WTH! It's not even playable out of the box, which is what you need for a quick, accessible filler.

King of Tokyo is the much superior game here sadly since it plays so smoothly. It's only redeeming quality is that it's cheaper than King of Tokyo (which is overpriced).

=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 6
I've only played Smash Up with my family, not with my gamer friends, so I can't speak to its depth. All I can say is that this game had the potential to be great, but did not get there. The artwork is great and the idea of shufflebuilding two factions and fighting over bases in the middle of the table is a compelling one. Only, it's never more than half realized. There is entirely too much text on the cards, meaning you spend most of your time reading cards instead of playing the game. This is a huge gripe for me, in general, because this could have been solved Race for the Galaxy style, by using icons and giving every player an excellent player aid. Also, the theme is only halfway integrated. Sometimes the powers of the cards are simply tacked-on to seem thematic, even though they don't impact the game. Also, it is entirely too long for its depth. It plays like a fighting game, but in reality it is a multiplayer game (you're not attacking each other directly; you're attacking the bases). This is a huge flaw because it actually means that the better everyone is doing (i.e., the most hotly contested the bases are), the longer the game will go on. That is simply bad design.
=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-

One of the few games I own that I prefer playing 2 players

RATING: 6
Whimsical card game. Take two factions, put them together, attempt to score areas on the board through hand management. On a turn play a minion and play an action, and follow the card text. I enjoy card games a lot, but I find this one to be lacking. Some turns are longer than necessary, whereas others are of without any imagination. If played at a reasonable pace this could be a decent filler game, but things can bog down and make it a longer game than necessary. There is potentially some balancing issues with the different factions, but even without it there are other card games I would prefer to play within the same time frame. Expansion adds more factions with unbalanced cards. Still a fun lighthearted game if you're not looking for heavy strategy.

RATING: 6

The gameplay is not BAD... but it isn't GOOD either.  A fairly pedestrian game, one that I would play, but would be very unlikely to suggest.

RATING: 8
This is a pretty enjoyable filler game that you play with a bunch of friends, or possibly complete strangers, between heavier games or at the end of night of gaming. Play time is pretty short, and the mechanics for the game are nothing special. What this game did do, ingeniously I might add, is have players select two different faction decks and shuffle them together creating all sorts of crazy comibinations and synergies. This is game is all about knowing how to make the most of your synergy between your two factions. If you rely too heavily on one faction you will probably get smocked for most of the game. But luckily like I said it will be over quickly. More factions will obviously make this game have even more permutations which is pretty high with the base game with only 8 factions to start with.
 
Be forewarned, those Gnomes are nasty little fuckers.

RATING: 5
I stayed away from Smash Up because its nerd-pandery nature turned me off. I really don't need any OMG EPIC BACON NINJA DEAD PARROT AWESOME PIRATE HOT SAUCE SHINY YOU SHALL NOT PASS boardgames. But I'd been told by others who don't tend to speak in catchphrases and movie quotes that the game play was pretty solid, so when a cheap copy came my way, I took a gamble.

It's not bad. Smashing together two factions is pretty neat, and I imagine there's a lot of fun in discovering combos within disparate factions (my Wizards and Robots worked very well together). There's a good game in here, and a lot of room for exploring it.

Unfortunately, it's not a good enough game. At its heart, Smash Up is one of those deploy-units-to-your-side-of-a-base-and-see-who-claims-it games and I've been through a number of those, with Omen: A Reign of War being the one to beat. I don't really need another one.

RATING: 4
This game is overrated like Munchkin, but at least Munchkin has some goofiness that made it fun.  This game can really drag out--of course it's random, who knows what will happen!  I don't like that you are given two decks randomly and certain decks work together much better than others.  Might as well just have everyone roll a die and whoever has the highest is the winner.

It's also really annoying to try to keep track of what all the bases do and what every card that's out there on bases do.  This game is the opposite of elegant.

RATING: 6
Type: 2-4 player competitive, smash-your-neighbor card game

Best with: 3-4?
Weight: Medium
Duration: 30-60 minutes
Notes:
heavily favors experienced players who already know cards/decks
card-based, not much text, but lots of effects to read, both in hand and placed on the boards
some turns can get complicated and long by a player
screw-your-neighbor quotient is high, especially for someone who gets ahead early

Smash Up is a card game for 2-6 players. Players pick two of the decks in the game and shuffle them together to create their deck for that round. For example, I can pick the Wizards and Zombies decks and combine them for a few games. During play, players play a card and draw a card. They play cards on bases set in the middle of the table. Each card played on a base will accrue points on that base. Once a base reaches a threshold value of points, that base blows up and is scored based on which player has the most points on that base. In the process, cards have various abilities and can be played to screw with your neighbors.

Just to be clear, this isn't a deckbuilding game (where you build your deck as you play) nor is this a customizable card game (where you build your deck at home and come to game night with your best creation). This game just has you pick two 20-card decks when you sit down, shuffle them together, and then smash your opponents' cards.

This ends up being a relatively quick game where you cycle through your given decks pretty quickly, and competition can get pretty fierce as players jockey for control of the bases. In fact, this game doesn't really provide players a chance to sit in a corner and just do their thing; there is constant competition and smashing of minions. Some people may be put off by the ruthless neighbor-bashing, but the game is so quick and the bashing such a prevalent thing, that pretty much everyone gets in on the action and gets hit with the stomping pretty constantly.

One upside to this game is the replayability is pretty high. Each of the base game's 8 factions plays slightly differently, and as such combine to play many different styles. 

There are some downsides to this game, though.

First, the game benefits from repeated play. Some of the card rules can be a bit hard to understand at first and may take some online research. Some sort of catalog of strange cards in an FAQ in the rules would have been crazy helpful. But once you get through all the cards a few times and nail down the rules, the game flows much smoother. However, this does take a while, even for a regular game group.

Second, there are so many rules on the cards! This means that new players will be lost by the time a few minions pepper the bases in the middle of the board. All the text on the cards is pretty much always in effect, so it can be very hard to track what is really going on at any given time. This can really bog down the experience for new players.

Third, the game can be played with 2 players, but really doesn't work nearly as well. You have only 2 bases to fight over, and every neighbod-stomping mechanic *has* to go against the other player, so it can be *very* confrontational. There are many more enjoyable 2-player games out there, even among the direct competition stomp-you-opponent type (Magic, Star Realms, any LCG, etc) that can scratch the card game itch.

Overall, this is a fun, light game when taken in quick doses for some neighbor-stomping fun. Just make sure to keep the game moving and not get bogged down in having too many cards in play that players can paralyzed trying to read everything and piece out plays.

Similar games in my collection: There really isn't anything quite as direct and neighbor-stomping as this game in my collection.

RATING: 5
Again, a card game in a box that is too big (where did I see this before, *wink*).

There is even room for more cards. Very nice of the publisher to make it so obvious, this game is going to cost more and more money, once you bought it.

Each turn, you play one or 2 cards from your hand in one of the 5 rows of cards already on the table. After a while that means, a lot of cards are on the table, with a lot of text on them. That means, to know what to play next, you need to reread all the cards on the table regularly, in every turn. Duh? Ok, sometimes a row of cards is resolved and removed, but where is the fun? If I want to read a lot, a read an interesting book.

When playing, i had to think about Smallword. Also a game with races and their specific features, but one that I enjoyed playing

Minus: 3 (game length) - 5 - 7 - 8 - 10

RATING: 4
Too much text on the cards makes it very hard to keep track of the current game state.  Perhaps some better iconography would have made the game flow better.

The game is very chaotic, which is not always a bad thing, but in this case it is because often you will have no good options.  If you have all action cards in your hand you will be stuck for a few rounds with weak choices.

I suppose the game is meant to be a filler with a ton of luck, but in that case it should be much shorter and snappier.  Turns take too long and you can't do a ton of planning while waiting because the game state will be much different by the time it gets back to you.

SmashUp! is a a dueling card game. The basic mechanics is that you have a hand of minions and actions, where minions have a value as well as possibly a card-defined effect, which are played on bases. The bases are worth points and are scored when the sum value of the minions played on it exceed its "breaking value"; generally the player with the highest minion sum value gets most points. The first to reach 15 points wins. That said in abstract, this is a game of extremes:

* Extremely cool concept - take all cool stereotypes and tropes and make decks out of them. Since you draft two factions per player you can f.i. have a pirate/ninja or undead/robot faction.

* Extremely and emminently simple rules, almost bordering on the minimalistic elegantness of German Euros. 

* Unfortunately also resulting in extremely slow games due to two major reasons: 
(1) the game requires constant counting and re-counting of base points. 
(2) Some decks are designed for repeated card drawing, reshuffling, deck manipulation and discard reorganisation, while others are very straigh-forward, resulting in extremely varying play and down times and for different player. These together brings out the worst from AP-prone players making a slow game even slower.

* Extremely disappointing delivery relative to what whas promised by its theme. 
(1) What should be a fast and furious jovial game becomes a slow and tedious bookkeeping extravaganza. 
(2) The mental demands made by this game is not of a complex or stimulating kind, it is of a simple even banale type that belies the investments of time and effort. It is it is slow and dry rather than fast and fun, and it is exhausting rather than entertaining.
=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-

RATING: 8.5
I play drastically differently depending on the group's experience level. The group I struggle with the most are beginners. It's easy to say "play a minion and action in either order, play one or the other, or none at all". After that, the idea of this being an easy to learn game falls flat. Players that know their factions' 20 card deck are leaps and bounds better than beginners. I struggle to find the right balance of explaining rules ahead of time versus explaining them when the situation arises. For example, base breaking and scoring procedures, talents, specials, on-going abilities and what to do when cards conflict.

Another big part of the learning curve is the factions themselves. I'll take the approach of saying "pick one you like". Based on their pick I would suggest a good pairing (much like a diner choosing a dinner and asking the waiter for a wine pairing) all while explaining the basic mechanics of the two factions, e.g. minion destruction, plays from the discard pile, benefits from being played with other minions at the same base. I like this approach best because the person is inherently mentally invested in their team.

In all the games that I've played, I can't recall a single four player game. I love the game with 2 and 3. It works well with both counts. I love that certain factions (many from the base game) that poop on your opponent in a two player game are naturally nerfed when a 3rd player is added. Looking at you Aliens.

50-75 additional plays w/ all expansions thrown in the mix

RATING: 7.6
Video Review: https://youtu.be/i_wi8MamuwY

Smash up is a game that uses a gimmick to it's max and actually works for it. Rather than having one faction vs another to claim bases, Smash up let's you smash together two factions to create Robot Sharks, Zombie Geeks, Pirate Robots and so on. 

Each turn you may play one minion and one action, although card powers often allow you to do more than that. 

It can be chaotic, especially when there are lots of cards on a base, and I probably would avoid playing 4 player, but overall it's great fun if you are in the mood.

RATING: 7
Smahs Up is a clever Deck Building game that takes the genre one step further by allowing the player to select any two themed decks to create a unique force. 

Fairy Dinosaurs, Robotic Ninjas, Pirate Zombies...you name it and it probably exists in the base game or one of the expansions. 

The aim of the game is to defeat a number of central bases in order to earn VPs. The trick is that any player can assign units to these bases to add their power to the attack. Once a base's defensive score is reached, the player with the greatest attack value earns the points (second and occasionally third can score too). 

So the players are constantly battling to get ahead at each base and some cards can destroy units as well. 

It really is a clever idea but there is a bit of take that in the play.

RATING: 5.5
Fun, man.

It's just quick and fun.

I printed the custom-made bases found on the files that takes away some of the constant hassle of counting the cards' powers.  I say some, because when you are playing with cards that give +1 power and cards that give -1 power, and cards that fluctuate in power depending on when they get played, and bases that alter power in so many ways...well, it gets confusing.

Update 1:  It is fun enough, but it has the potential of running for far longer than it should.  I also have no interest in the Cthulhu and Munchkin expansions.  I just don't know if this is a game I would want to play with any number of players knowing that there are better games in my shelves waiting to be played.  It is fun and casual at times, but is it really a good game?

Update 2: The constant tallying of scores makes it very dull.

RATING: 7
Each player gets two factions (out of eight possible) that are mixed up to form the players deck of 40 cards.
The aim is to score points by having your Minons control bases, aided by your Actions.

A simple and fast card game. Perhaps a tad to simple every now and then, but maybe not fast enough all the time.

Since my first play, I've been waiting for Smash Up to outstay its welcome, but keeps getting surprised when it doesn't.

Not sure how much skill is involved here, but since I tend to do well I'd like to claim that it's all skill. Picking what two factions to pair off is perhaps the biggest/only decision. Unfortunately, the factions could'v been better balanced.

An expansion or two might increase the score...

RATING: 5
Smash Up has a real Munckin-like feel, and I mean that in the worst possible way. Despite an attempt by AEG to make SU sound hilarious, the humor is forced. Actual gameplay is a dry affair that smacks of the Star Wars: CCG.

The artwork is very lovely though and players may feel like they should like SU just because it is so pretty, (much like Takenoko).

Pundits for SU say that the game gets better the more combinations available, and to not rush to judge until some of the expansions are added. Don't bother, the core gameplay won't change. Plus, even a cursory glance will tell you that some expansions are far worse than others; I'm looking at you Cthulhu expansion. As is, some of the combinations already available in the core set are really fiddly and make for long waits for the other players. Games drag on for way too long.

RATING: 6.5
Very light game with some strategic factor that becomes overshadowed by the chaos generated by the multiple players (the more players, the more chaos). This chaos though, is what makes the game fun. 

It can be a nice gateway game, especially if played with the right people. 

The key of the game are the special abilities of the cards, and this is 100% text, with no icons. Idiom is a huge barrier for this game.


I have the impression that the game is not very well balanced (zombies seem to be very powerful). If that turns to be true, I will reduce my rating. 

Edit (March 14): After the second game, I start to see some possible balance issues: ninjas are great because of Shinobi's ability... It gives many, many unexpected points to the user. I don't see ways to counter it.

The game is still to slow paced. We end up with too many cards in our hands, this certainly slows the game.

I reduce the rating from 7 to 6.5

RATING: 7.5
I walked around this game at the store, online and in person, for months.

When I first saw it, I was really excited for it, but I heard a lot of negative reviews saying it was 'mathy' and was just a card laying game.

This game is amazing!  The swing backs and balance is actually really surprising!  I've played countless games and have won with each faction and each pairing I've made was tons of fun.

The game isn't mathy at all.  Lost Cities is mathy.  This game is great for anyone and even a gamer like me who prefers lengthy and character-based tabletops, I am always in favor of playing.

If you like the art on the box and enjoy the thought of smashing together two cliche factions to form an army, then get this game.  It really feels different everytime you play and the expansion '9000' really increases replay value.

In the end this game is very balanced [no faction feels over powered once you play all the factions; however wizards/robots has won the game for me every single time], a lot of fun, and the quality of art and cards is amazing.

[COLOR=#FF0000]A year later... thoughts and rating (2):[/COLOR]

Since I only played this once I will stand by my original comments. In my opinion this is not a family game, nor is it very fun. [COLOR=#FF0000]Initial thoughts and rating (3):[/COLOR]

Just played with mt two oldest kids (10 and 7) and the game bombed. We played for 45 minutes and we had 2-3 points apiece. Way too much text on the cards for this game to be accessible to my 7 year old. She is a good reader, but having a hand of 5 - 10 cards with lots of text overwhelmed her. My son wasn't really enthralled with it either.

Both of my kids play and love Summoner Wars, but SU is not nearly as approachable nor would it have the depth of SW to play at a higher level with other skilled players.
So a huge thumbs down, I am really disappointed with this game.[/i]

RATING: 5
Smashing two 20 card decks together and seeing what happens, and how well they play together, is the exploratory hook. After that, it's your standard compete for majorities at different bases game (points for first, second and third), scored when cards of enough value have been played there. The card effects are very powerful so there's lots of kingmaking as cards get blown up left, right and centre. And if that levels everyone out by the time the end game arrives, then it's your standard lottery finish. As a result, the exploration angle to see what works well together isn't enough to draw me back, especially as it goes longer than games of this type should last.

RATING: 9
Super Fun! Fantastic card game for adults and kids, and for gamers and nongamers! Light card game, using your 2 unreal factions in playing out outrageous and creative combos against other unreal faction pairings and their outrageous and creative combos. Massive replayability. Cannot wait for expansions. 45 minute game. Better with 3 or 4 players.

Fantastic artwork and graphic design; really helps the feel/mood of the game. 

Same game designer who made Guillotine, another fantastic card game.


Have not tried the 2 box variant; I don't see how that can play out without problems.

The capture-the-base mechanic reminds me of that of Loot, but I love this game much much much more.

RATING: 5
This is a filler card game based on popular tropes, like ninjas, zombies, and dinosaurs.  Players randomly combined two of these factions before the game, and then played a take-that style game where you played cards to "base" cards and tried to be the first to a certain power threshold.  People were constantly destroying other people's cards, so this took longer than you might think.  Personally, I didn't think there was much of a game here; you basically just played what you drew.  Additionally, bad cards tended to accumulate in your hand, as there isn't a good way to cycle them, and the one-minion/one-action per turn rule sometimes was a big obstacle when you couldn't draw one or the other.  This wasn't really my style of game, and I don't think it was particularly well executed for the type of game that it is.

(2 plays)

RATING: 8
A solid tactical game for 4 players that surprised me with how much I enjoyed it. Expansion factions go from interesting to stupid real fast.

Pros:
* Excellent card quality.
* Nice art work.
* Interesting combinations.

Cons:
* Base cards are small and hard to read by all players.
* Failure to properly shuffle your deck (7 x riffle shuffle) can imbalance the game.
* Expansions include some of the worst genres in boardgaming (Steampunk, Cthulhu and Geeks ...WTF Pretty Pretty Smash Up?).
* I will never buy anything with the word "Geek" in it.

RATING: 9
As of 1/21/17
So I have held off purchasing this game for several years.  It seemed very gimmicky.  I own and have played Munchkin.  My younger son loves it, but Munchkin seemed to lose it's appeal rather quickly for me after the first few plays and getting over reading the humorous cards again and again. Replayability was lacking, at least for me, even though I will still play it occasionally.  So my concern with Smash Up was that this would be a similar type of game.

Wow was I wrong!  I watched a play through on Wil Wheaton's Tabletop which made it look fun, and I had a gift card to spend and decided to finally give it a try.  The first night my son and I played 3 back to back games which rarely ever happens with a new purchase.  We would have played more, but it was late and we were tired.

The next day at work I was thinking about the game and how I would love to try different faction combinations.  On the way home I stopped at my FLGS and picked up the "Awesome Level 9000" and the "Monster Smash" expansions.  I was that stoked as I am not a big expansion person. 

That night we played 4 more games mixing and matching factions.  I am still enjoying it and am going to get the wife to join us this weekend!  

What I like is:
--The asymmetrical factions 
--The large number of faction combinations
--Hitting combos and scoring when your opponent does not think you will (Reminds me a little of MtG)
--The player interaction 
--Foiling your opponents plans (I have plenty of Co-Ops when I am not feeling like a competitive game)
-- It plays fast so you can get in multiple games
--Most of all it is fun!!

What I do not like:
So far nothing really.  

As many forums state, some combos are more powerful than others.  Part of the fun though is picking out factions and seeing how to optimize them best.

We also draft the factions so you can use strategy there as well when playing trying to counter what opponents choose

As I log plays, so far they have all been close. I will update after more plays







.

=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 2
This is a cute idea in that you mash up two factions to get something silly, but gameplay wise it's sort of like Loot, but with massive downtime between turns. The game is essentially that there are these scoring cards in the center of the table. When the total numbers printed on cards players play on the scoring cards equals that card's printed durability the card scores points for whomever has the highest value in numbers. Add to that a lot of deckflip randomness in that many cards want other specific types of cards in order to preform their special abilities, but you either get that stuff or you don't, because the game doesn't wait around for you to draw what you need. Different factions have varying degrees of fiddilyness, which adds to the downtime, but didn't seem to add much depth to make up for it.

:star: Art and components
:nostar: Innovative mechanics
:nostar: Handles 5 or more players
:nostar: Good with different player counts
:nostar: Low time between turns
:nostar: Comfortable complexity
:star: Re-playability
:nostar::nostar::nostar: Enjoyment

RATING: 7

Some of the faction combos are overpowered, which leaves some of the factions hanging out in the box more than others.  Not that it is bad that it works out that way, I just wish it had been play tested more.  The endless expansions are a little tedious, and I DESPISE the fact that some of them are meant to be played by themselves, rather than added to the base set (I'm looking directly at you, Obligatory Cthulhu Set)...But, can't fault them for variety, and for those who love the game, there's always going to be more to play...and buy.  Me?  I stopped after sci-fi.  The game is basically unchanged since the first set, and I just don't need more incremental expansions.

RATING: 8
A chaotic card game, similar to Small World in terms of combinable player powers (i.e. shuffle to types of creatures together and go for it), but features more direct conflict and lots (!) more exceptions to the relaitvely simple rules. All the possible combinations of races make for great replayability but it might take some time for players to learn the races' advantages by heart and play towards their respective strength. On the other hand, the thematic aspect of the game is a great laugh and I for one love the idea of Dinosaur-Ninjas facing off against Undead-Russians (riding bears). Not sure how balanced all the race combinations are and a lot depends on card draws, then again, the game I played felt very balanced.

RATING: 8
Well, I was guessing I'd be a sucker for the mashing-up of genres, and I was right - gotta love playing Dinosaurs and Cthulu vs Pirates and Ninjas.
Quite a bit of space for tactics during the game - I'm not sure how some of the overpowered cards and combos would work in a 2 player game, but as long as it's played casually the game should be a winner typically.

Rules clarifications and ideas:
*If a minion is [u]not[/u] in play -- in the hand, deck, or discard pile -- its power is the number printed on the card.
If a minion [u]is[/u] in play -- on the table, next to a base -- its power is its printed number plus or minus all modifications that apply to it. 
* -With 4 players, play with three bases
  -With 2 or 3 players, use an equal number of bases.
* For faster games, consider playing to 10, or 12 VP's.

RATING: 5
The game has a lot of fun, silly art. Easy to learn, but the bases can get confusing quick. The bases should be different sized cards, and I wish it came with some scoring components. You can download some helpful files from BGG to help you keep track though, which helps. Very easy to learn and teach, this is a solid start to a game night. However playing with more than 3 people, you can easily get lost in all the card text when you're trying to remember what every card on every base does. I suppose if you play enough and get used to all the cards you'll learn what they do and won't always have to read the cards, but as it stands, I just get exhausted when I play this.

RATING: 7
Interesting card game - which is better than I had expected it to be from reading about it here on BGG. The different decks have very different flavours which are quite interesting, and of course, each game you are picking 2 different decks to mix together to form your personal deck - this is the main "gimmick" of the game, and looks to me to make it quite fun and replayable. Add in different "bases" each with their own unique characteristics, and I can see this one getting plenty of play before it gets boring.

But there are issues which prevent me from rating this higher than 7. Namely, there have been a few rules issues which don't seem to be adequately addressed in the rulebook, and several of the decks (most notably the ninjas and the wizard-type ones) have some very weird effects which are hard to sort out in play, and has led to a bit too much downtime for my liking. But overall I'm impressed - more than I expected to be by this game.

RATING: 9
Smash Up is everything I love in a card game; it's fun, it's fast paced, it's silly enough that people rarely take it too seriously and let it upset them, while still being deep enough to be very engaging and strategic. Each of the game's 'factions' plays surprisingly differently and while there are some pairs that really shine, there's neither a combination of factions that simply doesn't work, nor is there one that feels broken.

As much as I love introducing people to Android: Netrunner or playing games like Magic with my buddies, the high cost of Magic and amount of time it takes to put together decks in Netrunner if both players don't own decks already (not to mention the 2 player restriction) can really slow things down. This is where Smash Up shines most. It can be taught in minutes, 'building' a deck with a good mix of flavor literally takes seconds, and the base game supports up to 4 players for $30. To me, Smash Up is a must have for any regular group of friends, or someone who runs a gaming group at their LGS.

RATING: 7
I can see why people don't like Smash Up.  It sits in that awkward place where it is marketed as a light marshmallow confection but in fact the gameplay is more demanding than that.  Said gameplay requires a good understanding of the relevant decks and how they operate.  This will lead to AP and to new players getting squashed if they have an inappropriate faction match up (e.g. Steampunk/Pirates vs Zombie/Dinosaurs).

It works well as a 2 player game but you really need to both be willing to try out new combinations and accept that you may get trounced a few times.  It is a bitter pill to swallow (as I found last play) but this is a good game.  The expansion really helps matters too.

RATING: 6.5
21-05-2015. Rated after 1 recent play. I played Smash Up years ago with 4 or 5 players and hated it. I played it again with 2 players and think the game is ok now.

You start by choosing two sides and shuffling the decks together. Both sides have minions and action cards. Minions give you strength at a location and often times a special ability. Actions either help you or annoy your opponent. 

The game revolves around fighting for control of location cards. Each location card shows you how many 'strength' the location needs to be scored.

The game is super simple. On your turn, you play an minion and attack card. When you reach the scoring point of a loation, the person with the most strength there gets most points and often times the special ability listed. Light-hearted fun.

As said, the game is fine. I don't hate it anymore and would play again. The artwork is gorgenous and the factions are cool. The game feels fillery.
=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
